  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_741ba62b-94e0-455a-9f02-522cf79725ef'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3290157143356284255">Only a handful of fictional characters are recognized by first name alone. Dean Koontz's Odd Thomas is one such literary hero who has come alive in listeners' imaginations as he explores the greatest mysteries of this world and the next with his inimitable wit, heart, and quiet gallantry.<br/><br/>Now Koontz follows Odd as he is irresistibly drawn onward, to a destiny he cannot imag</span>
  <span id="freeText3290157143356284255" style="display:none">Only a handful of fictional characters are recognized by first name alone. Dean Koontz's Odd Thomas is one such literary hero who has come alive in listeners' imaginations as he explores the greatest mysteries of this world and the next with his inimitable wit, heart, and quiet gallantry.<br /><br />Now Koontz follows Odd as he is irresistibly drawn onward, to a destiny he cannot imagine. The legend began in the obscure little town of Pico Mundo. A fry cook named Odd was rumored to have the extraordinary ability to communicate with the dead. Through tragedy and triumph, exhilaration and heartbreak, word of Odd Thomas' gifts filtered far beyond Pico Mundo, attracting unforgettable new friends - and enemies of implacable evil. With great gifts comes the responsibility to meet great challenges. But no mere human being was ever meant to face the darkness that now stalks the world - not even one as oddly special as Odd Thomas.<br /><br />After grappling with the very essence of reality itself, after finding the veil separating him from his soul mate, Stormy Llewellyn, tantalizingly thin yet impenetrable, Odd longed only to return to a life of quiet anonymity with his two otherworldly sidekicks - his dog, Boo, and a new companion, one of the few who might rival his old pal Elvis. But a true hero, however humble, must persevere.<br /><br />Haunted by dreams of an all-encompassing red tide, Odd is pulled inexorably to the sea, to a small California coastal town where nothing is as it seems. Now the forces arrayed against him have both official sanction and an infinitely more sinister authority...and in this dark night of the soul, dawn will come only after the most shattering revelations of all.<br /><br /> ©2008 Dean Koontz; (P)2008 Brilliance Audio</span>
  <a data-text-id="3290157143356284255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1173229674" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1173229674?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8140560-odd-hours">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=dean-koontz">dean-koontz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1173229674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9658332632202640002">If you are keeping a running tally if Dean Koontz novels with a golden retriever in them, add another hash mark for Odd Hours.<br/><br/>I continue to enjoy the Odd series, but my one complaint is that the pacing, the story, the motivations, the progress, etc. all feel a bit flat. Things are never a 10, they are never a 1, they are always just at 5 or 6. This is interesting because there is some stuff that happens that should be very intense, but it isn't. Some of this may be caused by the characterization</span>
  <span id="freeText9658332632202640002" style="display:none">If you are keeping a running tally if Dean Koontz novels with a golden retriever in them, add another hash mark for Odd Hours.<br /><br />I continue to enjoy the Odd series, but my one complaint is that the pacing, the story, the motivations, the progress, etc. all feel a bit flat. Things are never a 10, they are never a 1, they are always just at 5 or 6. This is interesting because there is some stuff that happens that should be very intense, but it isn't. Some of this may be caused by the characterization of Odd (who has never seemed all that plussed in even the strangest and most intense situations since book one). <br /><br />Also, I cannot tell if he gets into odd situations because of his name, or if his name is Odd because of the situations he gets into. He is just always dealing with the weirdest stuff!<br /><br />In summary, if you have read and enjoyed up through Brother Odd, keep on trucking with Odd Hours. But, don't expect much difference in the feel of the story (which may please some of you).</span>
  <a data-text-id="9658332632202640002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23712682?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23712682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11539830622911057095">This book was an absolute train wreck. Having been a fan of and read all 3 previous Odd Thomas novels, I was very disappointed with this book. <br/><br/>This novel could have been condensed to about 200 pages. There was way too much "filler information". I became frustrated when the plot would drag, and then as it seemed to be moving along, it would go off track once again. Maybe this was Koontz's intended style, but I found it too much and annoying.<br/><br/>I don't need a biography on Sinatra or a Wikipedia artic</span>
  <span id="freeText11539830622911057095" style="display:none">This book was an absolute train wreck. Having been a fan of and read all 3 previous Odd Thomas novels, I was very disappointed with this book. <br /><br />This novel could have been condensed to about 200 pages. There was way too much "filler information". I became frustrated when the plot would drag, and then as it seemed to be moving along, it would go off track once again. Maybe this was Koontz's intended style, but I found it too much and annoying.<br /><br />I don't need a biography on Sinatra or a Wikipedia article on the habits of coyotes. <br /><br />Odds sarcastic wit/humor was way overdone to the point it lost its effectiveness and became old. <br /><br />I also found many of the parts of this story very predictable. <br /><br />All and all, I'm not bashing Koontz as I've read many of his novels and have been a fan. But this book left a lot to be desired and I hope the next OT novel is greatly improved. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11539830622911057095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lori Whitwam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/715797-lori-whitwam"><img alt="Lori Whitwam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442535080p2/715797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22863461?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori Whitwam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori Whitwam" href="/user/show/715797-lori-whitwam">Lori Whitwam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/715797-lori-whitwam?shelf=popular-fiction">popular-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22863461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14875776219646008896">Three stars may be the fewest I'd ever give a Dean Koontz book. Koontz fans (of which I am one) love Odd Thomas and his unpredictable supernatural abilities, troubled but simple life, and drive to do good in the world. This installment in the Odd Thomas saga, though, fell a bit short of the mark. <br/><br/>There are wonderful passages - Koontz has an amazing gift for description that is never cliche or vague. But this is one of the books in which the entire story takes place in just one day. I don't care </span>
  <span id="freeText14875776219646008896" style="display:none">Three stars may be the fewest I'd ever give a Dean Koontz book. Koontz fans (of which I am one) love Odd Thomas and his unpredictable supernatural abilities, troubled but simple life, and drive to do good in the world. This installment in the Odd Thomas saga, though, fell a bit short of the mark. <br /><br />There are wonderful passages - Koontz has an amazing gift for description that is never cliche or vague. But this is one of the books in which the entire story takes place in just one day. I don't care for this because it necessitates painfully long segments in which Odd's every thought and step, every tiny nuance of what he sees, hears, smells, or wonders must be explored. <br /><br />Also, Odd is away from Pico Mundo, and even from the monastery where he spent the last book, because he is frequently "called" somewhere to prevent an unknown atrocity. He usually has a fascinating, eclectic cast of supporting characters, but they were weaker than usual in this book. I totally don't get Annamaria, and I didn't appreciate the vague allusions at the conclusion suggesting some possible tie to his lost love, Stormy Llwellyn. <br /><br />The plot was OK, but hasn't the "scary, maniacal terrorist" thing been a bit done to death? And it clearly ended with the next novel already set up, which makes for a very unsatisfying end to the current one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14875776219646008896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer22672863&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22672863" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13047173424982449249">I was excited to see that Koontz had written another Odd Thomas book - I like the character, and I find his paranormal abilities fascinating. But this was by far my least favorite of the OT books. While this one has an interesting premise (Odd is drawn to the small coastal town of Magic Beach, CA by apocalyptic nightmares), I found the execution very lacking. <br/><br/>Again, Koontz really needs to cut down on "witty" dialogue. It just isn't as clever or endearing as he thinks it is. Increasingly, I find </span>
  <span id="freeText13047173424982449249" style="display:none">I was excited to see that Koontz had written another Odd Thomas book - I like the character, and I find his paranormal abilities fascinating. But this was by far my least favorite of the OT books. While this one has an interesting premise (Odd is drawn to the small coastal town of Magic Beach, CA by apocalyptic nightmares), I found the execution very lacking. <br /><br />Again, Koontz really needs to cut down on "witty" dialogue. It just isn't as clever or endearing as he thinks it is. Increasingly, I find myself just skimming long exchanges, whether they're between friends or foes, because they don't add to the story. Given the urgency of the situation in this book, there was just far too much of it.<br /><br />Second, I did not care for the open-ended way Koontz closes this book. We deserved to get more of an explanation of who or what Annamaria is. I didn't find her enigmatic, I found her annoyingly cliche and poorly written. She struck me as a waste of time, as she didn't factor into this story, truly. All the open threads only left me frustrated, NOT looking forward to the next book.<br /><br />And really...poltergeist!Sinatra? Really, Dean? </span>
  <a data-text-id="13047173424982449249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_15712237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15712237" />
    <a title="Echo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/851657-echo"><img alt="Echo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201652181p2/851657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15712237?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Echo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Echo" href="/user/show/851657-echo">Echo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/851657-echo?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15712237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16283533635883999701">Just as fabulous as I expected out of the Odd Thomas series. Koontz even manages to reference another of his novels, not at all related to the world of Odd Thomas, if you catch it. In the beginning Odd is wearing a sweatshirt with the words "Mystery Train" across the front that he got at "a thrift store". Die hard Koontz fans will recognize the Mystery Train from Christopher Snow's world in "Seize the Night". Does this mean Snow and Odd might eventually cross paths? There's something I would lik</span>
  <span id="freeText16283533635883999701" style="display:none">Just as fabulous as I expected out of the Odd Thomas series. Koontz even manages to reference another of his novels, not at all related to the world of Odd Thomas, if you catch it. In the beginning Odd is wearing a sweatshirt with the words "Mystery Train" across the front that he got at "a thrift store". Die hard Koontz fans will recognize the Mystery Train from Christopher Snow's world in "Seize the Night". Does this mean Snow and Odd might eventually cross paths? There's something I would like to read.<br /><br />Anyway, trivia aside, Odd continues to hold the heart of his reader with his utter lack of guile &amp; lovely habit of editing the bad languange of everyone around him. Koontz has definitely found us a hero we can love without any reserve.<br /><br />There is a definite cliff-hanger at the end of this book, promising us that our love-affair with Odd need not end yet. The questions of who exactly is Annamarie, how were those prarie dogs more than what they were, &amp; will Odd ever be reunited with Stormy will keep me in suspense of the next.<br /><br />The action was a little more fast-paced in this novel than I usually like &amp; there was a real lack of development of any characters other than Odd, which kind of bothered me. I missed Odd's friends in Pico Mundo although I loved the addition of Boo &amp; Frank Sinatra. Although, I have to say I loved Elvis more, but perhaps only because he was so much more developed &amp; involved in Odd's world. Not even Sinatra was able to break through the fast-pace of this book.<br /><br />Although I loved the book, I think Koontz kind of hurried through writing it &amp; I missed the great characters &amp; deep thought that usually goes into his books. I hope that in the next one Sinatra will develop into someone we can love &amp; Boo (&amp; Raphael) will hold more of a place than getting Odd out of only one mess. It wasn't nearly as good as Brother Odd, but we'll give you one more chance to redeem yourself, Koontz, before we lambast you for just selling the commercial-ness Odd.<br /><br />Still worth the read, though, Odd lovers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16283533635883999701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45159727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45159727" />
    <a title="Bob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/914102-bob"><img alt="Bob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442474476p2/914102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45159727?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob" href="/user/show/914102-bob">Bob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45159727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10502374637015723478">Occasionally great writers, like Dean Koontz, find a niche, which fits them so well that they rise above their already lofty status to produce works, which define them. Dean Koontz has done this with his Odd Thomas series. Like Stephen King with his Dark Tower Books, Koontz accomplishes this feat – in my opinion – with his incredible understanding of the lead character and his world.<br/><br/>In, Odd Hours, Koontz explores two of America’s biggest internal threats – greed and extreme idealism – and pits h</span>
  <span id="freeText10502374637015723478" style="display:none">Occasionally great writers, like Dean Koontz, find a niche, which fits them so well that they rise above their already lofty status to produce works, which define them. Dean Koontz has done this with his Odd Thomas series. Like Stephen King with his Dark Tower Books, Koontz accomplishes this feat – in my opinion – with his incredible understanding of the lead character and his world.<br /><br />In, Odd Hours, Koontz explores two of America’s biggest internal threats – greed and extreme idealism – and pits his hero, Odd Thomas, against a cast of all-too-close-to-home villains that will have you wondering about the guy who picks up your trash, and even that nice lady from church who gives so much of herself to help those in need. <br /><br />I found the ending of Odd Hours – which left me wondering about the fate of the various would-be assassins, and curious as to what “else” were those coyotes – a bit anticlimactic, but the wonderful characterization and suspenseful, adventurous setting more than make up for this. <br /><br /> – Bob Avey, author of the Detective Elliot Series<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10502374637015723478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_218733696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218733696" />
    <a title="Angela Oliver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5594267-angela-oliver"><img alt="Angela Oliver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465238878p2/5594267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218733696?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela Oliver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela Oliver" href="/user/show/5594267-angela-oliver">Angela Oliver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5594267-angela-oliver?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218733696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2493498577475329857">Another Koontx book that feels rather like he typed it up on the weekend, glanced over it once and thought "she'll be right". Like the previous Odd books, this contains some clever language and some rather entertaining non-cliches in Odd's thoughts. This is probably its saving grace. But, also like other Koontz novels, this contains bad guys with poorly explained motives, a pretty weak plot and despite what the "Observer" review says on the back, does NOT contain a "terrific final twist" or if i</span>
  <span id="freeText2493498577475329857" style="display:none">Another Koontx book that feels rather like he typed it up on the weekend, glanced over it once and thought "she'll be right". Like the previous Odd books, this contains some clever language and some rather entertaining non-cliches in Odd's thoughts. This is probably its saving grace. But, also like other Koontz novels, this contains bad guys with poorly explained motives, a pretty weak plot and despite what the "Observer" review says on the back, does NOT contain a "terrific final twist" or if it did, I blinked and missed it.<br /><br />Oh, and there's a golden retriever in it. I can understand that Koontz is very fond of dogs and the loyalty they provide. But does that mean that one needs to be inserted into every story? Boo the ghost dog is pretty neat, do we really need a mortal dog along for the ride? And what's with the pregnant woman? How's she related to Stormy, if at all? Well, don't go reading this book looking for answers. 'Cos you won't find them unless they're hiding between the lines (and quite frankly, I was in too much of a hurry to get the dratted thing finished to go looking for it).</span>
  <a data-text-id="2493498577475329857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_73176171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73176171" />
    <a title="Jak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1044380-jak"><img alt="Jak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1207055562p2/1044380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73176171?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jak" href="/user/show/1044380-jak">Jak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007267538" href="/book/show/2306609.Odd_Hours">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Absolutely no one. Not even Kootz fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer73176171&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73176171" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13267538470354356195">I’m sorry but this was truly awful. Not just Koontz’s worst Odd book but one of his worst, period. I’m struggling to think of any redeeming feature.<br/><br/>For starters the pace of the book was all wrong seemingly going slow slow quick slow slow. This is because very little actually happens in the first 300 pages and the reader is presented with overly long descriptive narrative and Odd Thomas ‘philosophy’. The plot itself was like something the production team of 24 rejected and throwing in a supernatu</span>
  <span id="freeText13267538470354356195" style="display:none">I’m sorry but this was truly awful. Not just Koontz’s worst Odd book but one of his worst, period. I’m struggling to think of any redeeming feature.<br /><br />For starters the pace of the book was all wrong seemingly going slow slow quick slow slow. This is because very little actually happens in the first 300 pages and the reader is presented with overly long descriptive narrative and Odd Thomas ‘philosophy’. The plot itself was like something the production team of 24 rejected and throwing in a supernatural element to it just makes it laughable. At least in 24 (which is generally speaking ridiculous plot wise) there is at least a sense of imminent and impending danger. The Nukes in Odd Hours are scheduled to go off for months. Hardly one minute to midnight stuff.<br /><br />Koontz tried to install wit and verve via Odd but it was all cringe worthy and over done. For the first huddled or so pages every paragraph would end with and Odd witticism. It would have been too much had they been good but as they were awful it made things cringe worthy. Worse yet it turns Odd, one of Koontz best loved characters, into an imbecile and is no way makes you feel sympathetic to Odd as you should. <br /><br />The dialogue was sub-standard and clunky and Koontz usual cast of characters put in an appearance. Some one disabled with indomitable spirit and inner beauty and the ubiquitous dog. With Elvis having passed over in Brother Odd what could Koontz do for a bit of showbiz cool? Surely he would not try to rehash an idea that was original at first but had got tired and was rightly pensioned off before it became annoying….. oh but he did.<br /><br />So this time with have Ol’ Blue Eyes himself Sinatra!!! YAY! Strange hoe Odd is never shadowed by the 5th Beatle or some one hit wonder huh? No, just music royalty for the lad from Pico Minto. And as for Odd winding him up to turn him into poltergeist Sinatra…. This has to be one of the weakest plot twists ever<br /><br />Then there is Annamaria. What was the point of her? She did absolutely nothing for the plot or Odd during the book and was only there clearly as an introduction for the next Odd book. Koontz tried to make her enigmatic and mysterious but she was basically very annoying, smug and incredibly unhelpful never answering a strait question. And I can’t believe that anyone will not have already worked out this spoiler but she’s clearly the living embodiment of Stormy Llewellyn. <br /><br />Then we get to the ending…oh dear god, please no. Koontz kept painting himself into a corner with Odd trapped by a bad guy. So in comes bad guy number 2 and shots the first bad guy. But wait, Odd is now covered by Bad guys 2. What to do? I’ve got it!! Bad guys 3 enters and shots bad guy 2! Ta da! Oh wait, Odd is still trapped with a bad guy. I know, here’s a twist that no one will ever guess! Enter bad guy 4 and guess what!!!! You’ll never get it, honest. Not in a million years…… bad guy 4 shoots bad guys 3! Seriously, utter genius and startlingly original never been done before stuff! Hmmmm wait a mo, that didn’t quite work out how I expected. Odd is still trapped and covered by a bad guy. Ah screw it, I’ll have Odd shot the bad guy and walk free.<br /><br />Oh and the bomb plot was largely facilitated by a disillusioned priest. Well I guess it makes a change from fiddling with the alter boys. <br /><br />The book itself has absolutely no resolution and leave more lose ends than I have ever encountered in a book. You know nothing more about the mysterious Annamaria than you did at page one. You have no uncovering of the shadowy forces that instigated the bomb plot. Odd doesn’t not grow or evolve as a character. <br /><br />At best the book is a hugely weak and superfluous set up for a 5th instalment of Odd Thomas. However, it genuinely feels like Koontz was told he had 30 day before his next book was due, had nothing on the slate so banged out an Odd book as fast as he could. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13267538470354356195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9166541471982473345" style="display:none">I hate giving this book two stars, because I LOVE Odd Thomas. He is one of my favorite fictional characters. This novel was as well written as Koontz novel's usually are, with those wonderful turns of phrase ... it just didn't seem as pulled together. I thought at first it was an exercise in developing Odd's character further. But Odd is what he is. Finally, after completing the novel, I thought that perhaps there is a Part II coming on it's heels, because there was much unfinished business. "All things in their time," as the character Annamaria says. But clearly Koontz did not intend for us to understand all things in the time it took to read this novel.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22996289" />
    <a title="Patrick O&#39;Neil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1187959-patrick-o-neil"><img alt="Patrick O&#39;Neil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1211836747p2/1187959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22996289?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick O&#39;Neil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick O&#39;Neil" href="/user/show/1187959-patrick-o-neil">Patrick O&#39;Neil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Koontz or Odd Thomas Fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22996289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17466191866720159674">Title: Odd Hours<br/>Author: Dean Koontz<br/>Fiction/Non-Fiction: Fiction<br/>Genre: Suspense/Horror<br/>Date Started Book: July 4, 2008<br/>Date Finished Book: July 9, 2008<br/><br/>Before Reading:<br/><br/>What do I expect to gain from reading this?<br/>I am already a fan of the Odd Thomas series; I was looking to continue Odd's adventures. <br/><br/>During/After Reading:<br/><br/>Brief Overall Summary of the Book:<br/>Odd has returned from the monastery of Brother Odd, the previous book, and has settled in the little coastal town of Magic Beach. He has a premonition</span>
  <span id="freeText17466191866720159674" style="display:none">Title: Odd Hours<br />Author: Dean Koontz<br />Fiction/Non-Fiction: Fiction<br />Genre: Suspense/Horror<br />Date Started Book: July 4, 2008<br />Date Finished Book: July 9, 2008<br /><br />Before Reading:<br /><br />What do I expect to gain from reading this?<br />I am already a fan of the Odd Thomas series; I was looking to continue Odd's adventures. <br /><br />During/After Reading:<br /><br />Brief Overall Summary of the Book:<br />Odd has returned from the monastery of Brother Odd, the previous book, and has settled in the little coastal town of Magic Beach. He has a premonition of a large number of deaths, which are somehow related to "The Woman of the Bell," a pregnant woman who he has seen on the pier. He named her thus because she wears a bell necklace around her neck. Odd goes to the pier, finds the woman, talks to her and finds her to be very nice, but very cryptic, and then meets three thugs. He convinces Annamaria, which is the woman of the bell's first name, to leave the pier and let him handle the thugs. When one of the thugs touches him, Odd and the thug (who we later learn is named Utgard (the name seems to be related to the Norse giants) also experiences the dream. In the confusion, Odd jumps off of the pier and escapes.<br /><br />Odd uses his "psychic magnetism" power to find Annamaria, who asks him if he will die for her. To his surprise, he says yes and becomes her protector. He takes her to his friend Birdie, and older lady who was deformed by her drunken father as a child. Birdie agrees to watch after her while Odd takes care of saving the world from the death he saw.<br /><br />Odd goes to the house of a man who assaulted him on the beach after he had escaped from the first band of thugs, and finds the man dead in his house, with a woman. The sprit of the dead man appears, and is very upset. Shortly after appearing, the mirror reaches out and grabs the spirit, and takes him, presumably to hell. Odd very briefly sees a terrible face in the mirror. Odd speculates that spirits that are going to be punished rarely wait around in this world for very long because they owe a debt, and can't escape paying it. Odd leaves the house quickly through a window as the police arrive. In the backyard he runs into a fence in the dense fog, alerting the police of his presence, and escapes them, with the help of a Golden Retriever he meets along the way. Odd runs to a church.<br /><br />In the church he meets the minister, who counsels him, but the minister calls the police because he recognizes the dog. The policeman who comes is the chief of police, who is scary, big, and mean. He takes Odd to jail to interrogate him, but not before Odd can hide his wallet (and the wallet of the dead man) in the church.<br /><br />Odd is being interrogated, and he discovers that Hoss Shakleton, the Police Chief, thinks that he and Annamaria are some secret agents, here to stop his plan to blow up four nuclear bombs in cities in the US. Odd plays along, and even pretends to be interested in helping Shakleton and make a lot of money, but then he escapes with the help of the ghost of Frank Sinatra, who has been following Odd since Elvis left him to move on to the next life. Odd taunts Sinatra into becoming a poltergeist, and uses this time to escape the Chief and Utgard, who has joined him in the interrogation room.<br /><br />Odd stows aboard the boat going to get the nukes, kills (much to his dismay -- he didn't ever want to kill anyone, but had no choice; he feels that he did not murder, he killed for the greater good) the thugs on the boat, beaches the boat, and calls the FBI and Homeland Security to take care of the nukes. At the end of the book, he runs into the Chief again when he goes to get his wallet, and narrowly escapes him when he is killed by one of the thugs from the beginning of the book. The preacher also kills his wife (they were also in on the scheme.) Odd is also forced to kill the other thug at the church, in order to escape. In and around the church, Odd encounters coyotes (for the second time in the book) and at first runs from them, but eventually escapes them by telling them to leave, and that they did not belong there, as Annamaria did during the first coyote encounter. This does not work until Odd touches the bell pendant, which Annamaria had given him in the beginning of the book. Annamaria told Odd earlier that the coyotes were what they seemed and more; since we did not see Bodachs in this book, I suspect that the coyotes may have been Bodachs in disguise. <br /><br />The book ends with Odd leaving with Annamaria (who seems to know a lot about Odd's past with his "Lost Girl Stormy," and even calls him "Odd One," as Stormy did in the first book.) Birdie says that she will join them later, and they drive away. Odd has a mental breakdown because of all of the killing, and Annamaria reassures him that he has saved entire cities. On the last page of the book is a copy of the card that Odd had gotten from a gypsy fortune teller machine with Stormy in the first book, which reads "You Are Destined to Be Together Forever."<br /><br />Interesting things about the book's structure:<br />The book is structured like any Odd Thomas book; it is suspenseful. Often times I never saw a surprise coming, but once it came I can't believe I missed it! <br /><br />Recurring images/themes/other things:<br />Coyotes; Odd wanting to see Stormy in the afterlife, but not wanting to die, as he loves life; Hope, and "the lake of abiding hope," where he and Stormy had once gone.<br /><br />What I thought of the book:<br />Awesome. I can't wait for the next one -- this seems to be setting up apocalyptic adventures to come! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17466191866720159674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_59292644" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59292644" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1342790-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311206862p2/1342790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59292644?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1342790-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59292644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18419846671635357572">I got locked out of my place the other night, and the friend who has our spare keys wasn't around. So I went to the drugstore and bought this book, then headed to the nearest sushi restaurant to kill time with some rolls, booze, and this book.<br/><br/>Let's just get this out of the way right now. This book is not good at all. It is terrible. But it was *so* terrible that it became funny and eventually I couldn't wait to see exactly how much more dreadful writing the author could pack into the rest of it.</span>
  <span id="freeText18419846671635357572" style="display:none">I got locked out of my place the other night, and the friend who has our spare keys wasn't around. So I went to the drugstore and bought this book, then headed to the nearest sushi restaurant to kill time with some rolls, booze, and this book.<br /><br />Let's just get this out of the way right now. This book is not good at all. It is terrible. But it was *so* terrible that it became funny and eventually I couldn't wait to see exactly how much more dreadful writing the author could pack into the rest of it. So the book itself is one star, but the looking forward to the remaining horrible-ness bumps it up to two stars.<br /><br />For starters, Dean Koontz keeps making his main character bring up Shakespeare. Obviously, Mr. Koontz would like me to start drawing comparisons in my head between his writing (which, as mentioned above, is execrable) and Shakespeare's. To paraphrase, I have read Shakespeare and Dean Koontz is no Shakespeare. <br /><br />Dean Koontz also likes to make his character talk about how other authors have written things really badly, thus elevating his main character above such terrible writing. It is terribly conceited and pompous and self-absorbed, and just plain off the mark. Given that this is one of the most horribly written books that I've read in the last few years.<br /><br />Just to let everyone know exactly how bad this book is -- I can't tell you which is worse: this or The Da Vinci Code. Does that make everything perfectly clear? <br /><br />I could go on and on about all the horrible tics this author uses, but I'll just stop here. <br /><br />If you're locked out of your place, spend your $10 on a crappy romance novel instead. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18419846671635357572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1600375244" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600375244" />
    <a title="Maggie K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2904850-maggie-k"><img alt="Maggie K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293725132p2/2904850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600375244?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie K" href="/user/show/2904850-maggie-k">Maggie K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600375244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16608315870786233111">ok, I really like Odd Thomas a lot, I think he is just a beautiful person. But this book was soo.....I don't know the word, but I got the feeling the author sat and wrote it all in one take, probably in one night, and then never looked at it again.<br/>First, it all takes place in the space of one night. But incomprehensibly, it deals with an issue of global security. These two things just do not work together! <br/>Second, Odd's gift is psychic magnetism. He is drawn toward people who need him and just c</span>
  <span id="freeText16608315870786233111" style="display:none">ok, I really like Odd Thomas a lot, I think he is just a beautiful person. But this book was soo.....I don't know the word, but I got the feeling the author sat and wrote it all in one take, probably in one night, and then never looked at it again.<br />First, it all takes place in the space of one night. But incomprehensibly, it deals with an issue of global security. These two things just do not work together! <br />Second, Odd's gift is psychic magnetism. He is drawn toward people who need him and just can show up where he needs to be. Sometimes this really really smacks of Deus ex Machina. Here, he had an apocalyptic type dream, and followed his gift to a California coastal town, where he meets a girl he feels he needs to protect. She seems to know all about him and his gifts, but none of that is ever explained.<br />Third, it seems there is so much filler! In one of the scenes at the beginning, he has a feeling some tough guys are after her so he jumps off the pier to distract them. That's ok, but then there follows chapters and chapters of how he climbed back up the pier and got away from them. kinda. It just seemed like so much filling, it was ridiculous!<br />Then, there are pages and pages of Odd's thoughts. This would be okay if he was analyzing the situation at hand, trying to figure out his role in this drama, but it wasn't. It was meandering thoughts about Stormy, and his parents, and Frank Sinatra, and his powers. Filler, filler, filler.<br /><br />The thin story line, the flat characterization of the girl, and the obviously overused psychic powers really put a dent in enjoying this novel. However, Odd's natural sweetness and beautiful character save the book to an acceptable level.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16608315870786233111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1469923884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6514278114858535586">So, I needed a break from the awesome <i> City on Fire </i> and this was available from the library for immediate digital download. So I downloaded. I am not sure why, probably because it is sort of like mind candy, but I have to say that I do not think I will following up with the rest of the books in the Odd Thomas series.<br/><br/>While I appreciated that Koontz stopped telling us all the details of the earlier books, just in case we were new to the series and fit the backstory tidbits more fluidly into <i> Odd </i></span>
  <span id="freeText6514278114858535586" style="display:none">So, I needed a break from the awesome <i> City on Fire </i> and this was available from the library for immediate digital download. So I downloaded. I am not sure why, probably because it is sort of like mind candy, but I have to say that I do not think I will following up with the rest of the books in the Odd Thomas series.<br /><br />While I appreciated that Koontz stopped telling us all the details of the earlier books, just in case we were new to the series and fit the backstory tidbits more fluidly into <i> Odd Hours </i>, I just don't like the direction the series is taking. Instead of a bunch of one-off mysteries, for lack of a better term, it appears we are now gearing up for the apocalypse to come (yeah, yeah, I know that one of the books is called <i> Odd Apocalypse </i> so I guess I could have seen this coming). There is a mysterious organization, an evil Senator, and an enigmatic young woman who will somehow play some part on the side of good, which naturally is represented by our man Odd. Oh, and there will be a posse of other kooky characters backing him up. <i> Odd Hours </i> is the beginning of this journey. So, yeah.<br /><br />I just don't see how the quirky tone Koontz established in the early Odd books is going to work in this new arrangement, but since the novelty of Odd was playing out, I suppose this move may not be the worst idea. I mean how many ridiculous plotlines can one person who sees dead people face?<br /><br />Full review of the first three Odd Thomas books at my blog: <a href="http://lpolcar1.wix.com/readordie" rel="nofollow noopener"> Read or Die </a>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6514278114858535586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39052781?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsten" href="/user/show/1765276-kirsten">Kirsten</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1765276-kirsten?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39052781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8596015370078955254">So due to the newest Odd Thomas book coming out in a month, I decided to buckle down and force myself to read this book. Previously, I had stopped shortly after starting it, frustrated with the story and deciding that there was more I wanted to do with my time than read it. <br/><br/>Now that I made myself get past the horrible beginning and onto the tolerable middle and the dragging-on ending, I'm glad I read it. <br/><br/>That being said, this wasn't one of my favorites. I felt that Koontz whipped this one up on </span>
  <span id="freeText8596015370078955254" style="display:none">So due to the newest Odd Thomas book coming out in a month, I decided to buckle down and force myself to read this book. Previously, I had stopped shortly after starting it, frustrated with the story and deciding that there was more I wanted to do with my time than read it. <br /><br />Now that I made myself get past the horrible beginning and onto the tolerable middle and the dragging-on ending, I'm glad I read it. <br /><br />That being said, this wasn't one of my favorites. I felt that Koontz whipped this one up on a spur of the moment hankering one weekend and didn't bother to give it any depth or life. I still stand by my feelings that the title "Odd Hours" was merely another excuse to have a catchy title rather than a well-written book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8596015370078955254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zudYPGRuA1BQ/o1a/k03dVfvQJla/tT4nYtxOnUX8F7eVv+r1vyrr8XBYy0VELmUiAjoW/1KsxKzjXyal/Zbag==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dDHVNAx4W6FtvpKEHaGIfeHijdolANrX/SnPv/VpdXBkgHKjvurzXviBfPP2/AacPgUlGIK0vT3TL8IfF4jeRA==')})
  }

For this was a favorite phrase of Stormy Llewellyn, his lost love, and Stormy is dead, gone forever from this world. In the haunted halls of the isolated monastery where he had sought peace, Odd Thomas is stalking spirits of an infinitely darker nature.\n\nThrough two New York Times bestselling novels Odd Thomas has established himself as one of the most beloved and unique fictional heroes of our time. Now, wielding all the power and magic of a master storyteller at the pinnacle of his craft, Dean Koontz follows Odd into a singular new world where he hopes to make a fresh beginning—but where he will meet an adversary as old and inexorable as time itself.\n\nSt. Bartholomew’s Abbey sits in majestic solitude amid the wild peaks of California’s high Sierra, a haven for children otherwise abandoned, and a sanctuary for those seeking insight. Odd Thomas has come here to learn to live fully again, and among the eccentric monks, their other guests, and the nuns and young students of the attached convent school, he has begun to find his way.       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2313023-odd-hours">Quotes from Odd Hours</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Grief can destroy you --or focus you. You can decide a relationship was all for nothing if it had to end in death, and you alone. OR you can realize that every moment of it had more meaning than you dared to recognize at the time, so much meaning it scared you, so you just lived, just took for granted the love and laughter of each day, and didn't allow yourself to consider the sacredness of it. But when it's over and you're alone, you begin to see that it wasn't just a movie and a dinner together, not just watching sunsets together, not just scrubbing a floor or washing dishes together or worrying over a high electric bill. It was everything, it was the why of life, every event and precious moment of it. The answer to the mystery of existence is the love you shared sometimes so imperfectly, and when the loss wakes you to the deeper beauty of it, to the sanctity of it, you can't get off your knees for a long time, you're driven to your knees not by the weight of the loss but by gratitude for what preceded the loss. And the ache is always there, but one day not the emptiness, because to nurture the emptiness, to take solace in it, is to disrespect the gift of life.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/79736-grief-can-destroy-you---or-focus-you-you-can-decide">1360 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Loss is the hardest thing, I said. But it's also the teacher that's the most difficult to ignore.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/127576-loss-is-the-hardest-thing-i-said-but-it-s-also">58 likes</a>
            </nobr>
